<p>The <b>Metropolitan line</b> is a <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> line that runs from <a href="/wiki/Aldgate" title="Aldgate">Aldgate</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Amersham" title="Amersham">Amersham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesham" title="Chesham">Chesham</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>, with branches to <a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uxbridge" title="Uxbridge">Uxbridge</a> in the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hillingdon" title="London Borough of Hillingdon">London Borough of Hillingdon</a>. Coloured <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">magenta</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> 235) on the <a href="/wiki/Tube_map" title="Tube map">tube map</a>, the line is 41.4 miles (66.7 km) in length and serves 34 stations. The section between Aldgate and Baker Street is shared with the <a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Circle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_%26_City_line" title="Hammersmith &amp; City line">Hammersmith &amp; City</a> lines; that between <a href="/wiki/Rayners_Lane_tube_station" title="Rayners Lane tube station">Rayners Lane</a> and Uxbridge with the <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_line" title="Piccadilly line">Piccadilly line</a>; and that between Harrow-on-the-Hill and Amersham with <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Railways" title="Chiltern Railways">Chiltern Railways</a>. Just under 67 million passenger journeys were made on the line in 2011/12. The line is one of only two London Underground lines to cross the Greater London boundary, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central line</a>.</p>
<p>In 1863 the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a> began the world's first underground railway between <a href="/wiki/London_Paddington_station" title="London Paddington station">Paddington</a> and Farringdon Street with wooden carriages and steam locomotives, but its most important route became the line north into the <a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a> countryside, where it stimulated the development of new suburbs. Harrow was reached in 1880, and the line extended as far as <a href="/wiki/Verney_Junction_railway_station" title="Verney Junction railway station">Verney Junction</a> in Buckinghamshire, more than 50 miles (80 km) from Baker Street. From the end of the 19th century, the railway shared tracks with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Central_Railway" title="Great Central Railway">Great Central Railway</a> route out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marylebone_railway_station" title="Marylebone railway station">Marylebone</a>. The central London lines were electrified by 1907, but electric locomotives were exchanged for steam locomotives on trains heading north of Harrow. After the railway was absorbed by the <a href="/wiki/London_Passenger_Transport_Board" title="London Passenger Transport Board">London Passenger Transport Board</a> in 1933 the line was cut back to <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury_railway_station" title="Aylesbury railway station">Aylesbury</a>. Steam trains ran until 1961, when the line was electrified to and services curtailed at Amersham. The Hammersmith &amp; City line was shown on the <a href="/wiki/Tube_map" title="Tube map">tube map</a> as part of the Metropolitan line until 1990, when it appeared as a separate line. The current <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_S7_and_S8_Stock" title="London Underground S7 and S8 Stock">S Stock</a> trains entered service between 2010 and 2012.</p>
<p>The track is underground between <a href="/wiki/Aldgate_tube_station" title="Aldgate tube station">Aldgate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finchley_Road_tube_station" title="Finchley Road tube station">Finchley Road</a>; unlike the tube railways, the tunnels are just below the surface (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cut_and_cover" title="Cut and cover">cut and cover</a>) and of similar size to those for mainline trains. <a href="/wiki/Baker_Street_tube_station" title="Baker Street tube station">Baker Street</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a> terminus for some trains, others continuing to Aldgate in the City. Most of the route is two tracks, except for the single-track <a href="/wiki/Chesham_branch" title="Chesham branch">Chesham branch</a> and a four-track section between <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Park_tube_station" title="Wembley Park tube station">Wembley Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moor_Park_tube_station" title="Moor Park tube station">Moor Park</a> that allows fast services to overtake slower trains. There are also four tracks between Wembley Park and <a href="/wiki/Finchley_Road_tube_station" title="Finchley Road tube station">Finchley Road</a>, but the inner pair of tracks was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Bakerloo_line" title="Bakerloo line">Bakerloo line</a> in 1939, then to the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line" title="Jubilee line">Jubilee line</a> in 1979, the trains on these lines calling at all stations. The Metropolitan line runs on the outer fast lines. The disused Metropolitan line platforms at Willesden Green and Neasden are still in place despite Metropolitan line services having been withdrawn in 1940.</p>
<p>The Watford branch is due to be diverted to <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction</a>, resulting in the closure of <a href="/wiki/Watford_tube_station" title="Watford tube station">Watford station</a> and the opening of two new stations.The extension will link up with the <a href="/wiki/London_Overground" title="London Overground">London Overground</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_DC_Line" title="Watford DC Line">Watford DC Line</a>. The Metropolitan line will provide interchange with the Overground at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_High_Street" title="Watford High Street">Watford High Street</a> before terminating at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_Junction" title="Watford Junction">Watford Junction</a> providing interchange with the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>. Construction is due to begin in 2016 and be completed by 2020.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Railway">Metropolitan Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="720" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png/220px-Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png/330px-Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png/440px-Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Constructing_the_Metropolitan_Railway.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Construction of the Metropolitan Railway close to King's Cross station in 1861</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a> (also known as the Met) was a passenger and goods railway that served London from 1863 to 1933, its main line heading north-west from <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">the City</a> to what were to become the <a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a> suburbs. Its first line connected the mainline railway termini at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paddington_railway_station" title="Paddington railway station">Paddington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="King's Cross railway station">King's Cross</a> to the City, built beneath the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Road_(London)" title="New Road (London)">New Road</a> using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cut-and-cover" title="Cut-and-cover">cut-and-cover</a> method between Paddington and King's Cross, and in tunnel and cuttings beside <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_Road" title="Farringdon Road">Farringdon Road</a> from King's Cross to near <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_London" title="Smithfield, London">Smithfield</a>. It opened on 10 January 1863 with gas-lit wooden carriages hauled by steam locomotives, the world's first underground railway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen19873.E2.80.935_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen19873.E2.80.935-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1871, when plans were presented for an underground railway in Paris, it was called the <i>Métropolitain</i> in imitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The modern word <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> is a short form of the French word.</p>
<p>The railway was soon extended from both ends and northwards via a branch from <a href="/wiki/Baker_Street_tube_station" title="Baker Street tube station">Baker Street</a>. It reached <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_tube_station_(Hammersmith_%26_City_and_Circle_lines)" title="Hammersmith tube station (Hammersmith &amp; City and Circle lines)">Hammersmith</a> in 1864 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond_station_(London)" title="Richmond station (London)">Richmond</a> in 1877, and completed the <i><a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Inner Circle</a></i> in 1884,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen19877.E2.80.9310_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen19877.E2.80.9310-5">[5]</a></sup> but the most important route became the line north into the Middlesex countryside, where it stimulated the development of new suburbs. <a href="/wiki/Harrow-on-the-Hill_station" title="Harrow-on-the-Hill station">Harrow</a> was reached in 1880, and the line extended as far as <a href="/wiki/Verney_Junction_railway_station" title="Verney Junction railway station">Verney Junction</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>, more than 50 miles (80 kilometres) from Baker Street. From the end of the 19th century, the railway shared tracks with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Central_Railway" title="Great Central Railway">Great Central Railway</a> route out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marylebone_railway_station" title="Marylebone railway station">Marylebone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198711.E2.80.9314_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198711.E2.80.9314-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Electric traction was introduced in 1905 with <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple units</a> operating between Uxbridge, Harrow-on-the-Hill and Baker Street. To remove steam and smoke from the tunnels in central London, the railway purchased <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway_electric_locomotives" title="Metropolitan Railway electric locomotives">electric locomotives</a>, exchanged for steam locomotives at Harrow from 1908.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198724.E2.80.9326_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198724.E2.80.9326-7">[7]</a></sup> In 1910, a seventeen-minute silent film recording was made showing large portions of the journey from Baker Street to Aylesbury and Uxbridge, seen from the cab of a train. The film survives and is publicly available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_Trip_on_the_Metropolitan_Railway_.281910.29_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-A_Trip_on_the_Metropolitan_Railway_.281910.29-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike other railways in the London area, the Met developed land for housing, thus benefitting from the increase in the value of its land caused by the building of the railway. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> it promoted its housing estates near the railway with the "<a href="/wiki/Metro-land" title="Metro-land">Metro-land</a>" brand.</p>
<p>To improve services, more powerful electric and steam locomotives were purchased in the 1920s. A short branch opened from Rickmansworth to Watford in 1925. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the 4-mile (6.4 km) Stanmore branch was built from Wembley Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198743.E2.80.9345_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198743.E2.80.9345-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="London_Transport">London Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: London Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_line_(1933%E2%80%9388)" title="Metropolitan line (1933–88)">Metropolitan line (1933–88)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg/220px-Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg/330px-Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg/440px-Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Railway_No_12_Sarah_Siddons_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Electric Locomotive No.12 "Sarah Siddons" seen at a heritage event at Amersham in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 July 1933 the Metropolitan was amalgamated with other Underground railways, tramway companies and bus operators to form the <a href="/wiki/London_Passenger_Transport_Board" title="London Passenger Transport Board">London Passenger Transport Board</a>, and a period of rationalisation followed. While the Metropolitan was run as an outer suburban route with steam-hauled trains and goods services, the LPTB wished to focus on electrified trains and suburban traffic. Goods services were passed to the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London and North Eastern Railway">London and North Eastern Railway</a>, which also took over the role of providing steam locomotives for trains beyond the end of electrification at Rickmansworth. All services north-west of <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury_railway_station" title="Aylesbury railway station">Aylesbury</a> were withdrawn by 1936<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198746.E2.80.9348_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198746.E2.80.9348-10">[10]</a></sup> though services returned to <a href="/wiki/Quainton_Road_railway_station" title="Quainton Road railway station">Quainton Road</a> between 1943 and 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne200369_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne200369-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1930s was a period of rapid growth for the north-western suburbs of London, and LPTB developed ambitious plans to simplify the Metropolitan line and expand capacity. Several stations on the Uxbridge branch were rebuilt, replacing temporary wooden buildings with modernist designs and giving Uxbridge station a new site in the town centre. A major bottleneck in the line, the double-track tunnel from Baker Street to Finchley Road, was bypassed by boring two tube tunnels underneath the Metropolitan tunnels, transferring slow services and the <a href="/wiki/Stanmore_tube_station" title="Stanmore tube station">Stanmore</a> branch to the <a href="/wiki/Bakerloo_line" title="Bakerloo line">Bakerloo line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198751_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198751-12">[12]</a></sup> (This route was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line" title="Jubilee line">Jubilee line</a> in 1979.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198763_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198763-13">[13]</a></sup> In 1936 the line was extended east from <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_station" title="Whitechapel station">Whitechapel</a> to <a href="/wiki/Barking_station" title="Barking station">Barking</a> along the tracks of the District line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup> London Transport inherited a number of incompatible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_units" title="Electric multiple units">electric multiple units</a> from the railway, including the 1927–33 multiple-unit compartment stock used on routes to Watford and Rickmansworth, and these were refurbished to form a uniform fleet and designated <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_T_Stock" title="London Underground T Stock">London Underground T Stock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce198372.E2.80.9374_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce198372.E2.80.9374-15">[15]</a></sup> In the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_F_Stock" title="London Underground F Stock">F Stock</a> trains, with sliding doors under the control of the guard, were transferred from the District line; these mainly worked the semi-fast Harrow and Uxbridge services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce198378.E2.80.9381_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce198378.E2.80.9381-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>A major rebuilding of the main line from Wembley Park to Amersham was planned in the 1930s but delayed by the war. The line from Wembley to Harrow was rebuilt immediately after the war and the project was completed from 1956-1962, on a more modest scale than originally planned. Until 1961, passenger trains continued to be attached to a steam locomotive at <a href="/wiki/Rickmansworth_station" title="Rickmansworth station">Rickmansworth</a> to run to Aylesbury. The rebuilding electrified the line from Rickmansworth to Amersham, transferring all Aylesbury services to British Railways. A pair of fast lines was added from Harrow to north of Moor Park by 1962, allowing outer-suburban trains to run fast to Moor Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198755_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198755-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (September 2014)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Aluminium <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_A60_and_A62_Stock" title="London Underground A60 and A62 Stock">A stock</a>, originally unpainted, replaced the T stock and locomotive-hauled trains. More A Stock trains were built in 1962–63 to replace the trains on the Uxbridge service, giving the main line a single train type for all services. A Stock was 4-car units that could operate as four- or eight-car trains;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce1983110_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce1983110-18">[18]</a></sup> normally operated as eight cars, a 4-car unit operated the Chesham shuttle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruce1983113_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruce1983113-19">[19]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Driver-only_operation" title="Driver-only operation">One person operation</a> of the trains was proposed in 1972, but due to conflict with the trades unions was not introduced on the line until 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_separate_identity">A separate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: A separate identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="439" data-file-width="640" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg/220px-Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg/330px-Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg/440px-Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rayner%27s_Lane_Station._-_geograph.org.uk_-_39714.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Stock vehicles at Rayners Lane in their original unpainted livery</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_London_line" title="East London line">East London line</a> had been an isolated shuttle since 1939,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup> it was shown on London Underground maps as part of the Metropolitan line until 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1970 it was shown with a thin white line in the middle and labelled the "East London section".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> By the 1985 map it had become the "East London Line", remaining the same colour as the Metropolitan line with a white line in the middle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> changed to orange by the 1990 map.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T90_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-T90-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1990 the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_%26_City_line" title="Hammersmith &amp; City line">Hammersmith &amp; City line</a> became a separate line from Hammersmith to Whitechapel (Barking during the peak), the Metropolitan line being from Aldgate to Baker Street and northwards to Amersham with branches to Uxbridge and Watford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T90_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-T90-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, the infrastructure was partly privatised in a <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public–private partnership">public–private partnership</a> managed by the <a href="/wiki/Metronet" title="Metronet">Metronet</a> consortium. Metronet went into <a href="/wiki/Administration_(law)" title="Administration (law)">administration</a> in 2007 and <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> took over responsibilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 December 2010 the service to Amersham was reduced from four trains per hour to two, and a direct service between Chesham and central London was introduced, replacing the 4-car Chesham to Chalfont &amp; Latimer shuttle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chesham_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chesham-26">[26]</a></sup> The final passenger services operated by the A Stock ran on 26 September 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> followed by a ticketed public <a href="/wiki/Railtour" title="Railtour">railtour</a> on 29 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Route">Route</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Route">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Map">Map</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Map">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:center; max-width:708px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Line_%26_London_map.svg" title="The route of the Metropolitan line through the Greater London Boroughs and the English Counties of Hertfordshire and Buckinghamshire. <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Line_%26_London_map.svg" title="File:Metropolitan Line &amp; London map.svg"></a></div>
The route of the Metropolitan line through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Boroughs" title="London Boroughs">Greater London Boroughs</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Counties" title="English Counties">English Counties</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buckinghamshire" title="Buckinghamshire">Buckinghamshire</a>. More details of the route between Baker Street and Aldgate are shown at <a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)#Map" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Circle line: Map</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_line">Railway line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Railway line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td style="padding:0;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
<table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="display: table; width: unset; line-height: 0; padding:0 !important; margin: 0 auto !important">

<p>The Metropolitan line is 42 miles (67 km) long and serves 34 stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Key_Facts_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Key_Facts-29">[29]</a></sup> It is electrified with a four-rail DC system: a central conductor rail is energised at –210 V and a rail outside the running rail at +420 V, giving a potential difference of 630 V.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin2012_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin2012-30">[30]</a></sup> The first 6 miles (9.7 km) from <a href="/wiki/Aldgate_tube_station" title="Aldgate tube station">Aldgate</a> are below ground,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Line_Facts_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Line_Facts-31">[31]</a></sup> shared with the <a href="/wiki/Circle_line_(London_Underground)" title="Circle line (London Underground)">Circle</a> and Hammersmith &amp; City lines to Baker Street, where the line diverges, remaining in tunnel until <a href="/wiki/Finchley_Road_tube_station" title="Finchley Road tube station">Finchley Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> Between Finchley Road and <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Park_tube_station" title="Wembley Park tube station">Wembley Park</a> the line runs parallel to the Jubilee line, the tracks being paired by direction, with <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform_interchange" title="Cross-platform interchange">cross-platform interchange</a> at the two stations. At Wembley Park the Jubilee line diverges to the Stanmore branch at a grade-separated junction. From just after Finchley Road these four tracks run parallel with the <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Main_Line" title="Chiltern Main Line">Chiltern Main Line</a> from <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_station" title="Marylebone station">Marylebone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between Wembley Park and <a href="/wiki/Harrow-on-the-Hill_station" title="Harrow-on-the-Hill station">Harrow-on-the-Hill</a> the Metropolitan is four-track, with fast and slow lines paired by direction, paralleling the two-track un-electrified Chiltern Main Line. The slow lines are between the fast lines, and the two intermediate stations have island platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> Harrow-on-the-Hill has platforms on all six lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> The central slow lines diverge here at a <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade-separated</a> junction to become the 7.5 miles (12.1 km) Uxbridge branch. After <a href="/wiki/West_Harrow_tube_station" title="West Harrow tube station">West Harrow</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Rayners_Lane_tube_station" title="Rayners Lane tube station">Rayners Lane</a> the line is joined by the <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_line" title="Piccadilly line">Piccadilly line</a>, which shares the tracks to Uxbridge; a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turnback" title="Turnback">turnback</a> siding allows some Piccadilly line services to terminate at Rayners Lane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003x_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003x-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the main line between Harrow-on-the-Hill and <a href="/wiki/Moor_Park_tube_station" title="Moor Park tube station">Moor Park tube station</a>, the line is four-track, paired by use. The western fast tracks are shared with Chiltern line services from Marylebone; the eastern slow tracks have platforms at the intermediate stations. There is access at Watford triangle to the Watford branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> This double-track branch has stations at <a href="/wiki/Croxley_tube_station" title="Croxley tube station">Croxley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watford_tube_station" title="Watford tube station">Watford</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> but in 2018 the Croxley Rail Link is scheduled to open, involving the closure of Watford station and diversion of the line to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_station" title="Watford Junction station">Watford Junction</a> via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_High_Street_tube_station" title="Watford High Street tube station">Watford High Street</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Croxley_plans_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Croxley_plans-34">[34]</a></sup> From the Watford triangle to <a href="/wiki/Amersham_station" title="Amersham station">Amersham</a> the line has two tracks. At <a href="/wiki/Chalfont_%26_Latimer_station" title="Chalfont &amp; Latimer station">Chalfont &amp; Latimer</a> the 3.89 miles (6.26 km) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_track_(rail)" title="Single track (rail)">single-track</a> <a href="/wiki/Chesham_branch" title="Chesham branch">Chesham branch</a> diverges, running parallel to the main line for a distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Key_Facts_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Key_Facts-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-map_32-7"><a href="#cite_note-map-32">[32]</a></sup> The Metropolitan line ends at Amersham, where there are turnback sidings just beyond the platforms. The route continues to <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury_railway_station" title="Aylesbury railway station">Aylesbury</a> with Chiltern Railways trains only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmCh_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmCh-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-disputed" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:System-search.svg"><img alt="System-search.svg" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="45" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/45px-System-search.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/68px-System-search.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/System-search.svg/90px-System-search.svg.png 2x" width="45"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b>factual accuracy is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">disputed</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help to ensure that disputed statements are <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliably sourced</a>. See the relevant discussion on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Metropolitan_line#Dispute" title="Talk:Metropolitan line">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(June 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The fast lines north of Harrow and all lines north of Rickmansworth are signalled with LUL signalling, but using four-aspect Network Rail signal heads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRS_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRS-36">[36]</a></sup> The upper two lights are a two-aspect stop signal displaying either a green or red aspect, the lower two lights a repeater signal for the next stop signal ahead showing a green or yellow aspect, or no aspect when the stop signal shows a red aspect. Thus they are effectively four-light three-aspect signals with green/red/green/yellow lights from the top, danger being a single red light, caution the top green light over a yellow light, and clear two green lights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRS_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-BRS-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Metropolitan Line is the only line to operate express service, though currently this is only southbound in the morning peaks and northbound in the evening peaks(Monday to Friday).</p>
<ul>
<li>Southbound Fast trains run non-stop from Moor Park to Harrow-On-The-Hill and Harrow-On-The-Hill to Finchley Road<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>Southbound Semi-Fast trains run non-stop between Harrow-On-The-Hill and Finchley Road<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Northbound Fast and Semi-Fast trains additionally call at Wembley Park<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The off-peak service in trains per hour (tph) presently consists of:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>2tph Amersham to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>2tph Chesham to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>4tph Watford to/from Baker Street (all stations)</li>
<li>7tph Uxbridge to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>1tph Uxbridge to/from Baker Street (all stations)</li>
</ul>
<p>The morning peak service in trains per hour (tph) presently consists of:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>2tph Amersham to/from Aldgate (fast)</li>
<li>2tph Amersham to/from Aldgate (semi-fast)</li>
<li>2tph Chesham to/from Aldgate (fast)</li>
<li>1tph Watford to/from Aldgate (semi-fast)</li>
<li>1tph Watford to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>3tph Watford to/from Baker Street (semi-fast)</li>
<li>3tph Watford to/from Baker Street (all stations)</li>
<li>2tph Uxbridge to/from Aldgate (semi-fast)</li>
<li>4tph Uxbridge to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>4tph Uxbridge to/from Baker Street (all stations)</li>
</ul>
<p>Note that southbound fast and semi-fast trains return as northbound all stations services in the morning peak with the same frequency.</p>
<p>The evening peak service in trains per hour (tph) presently consists of:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>2tph Amersham to/from Aldgate (fast)</li>
<li>2tph Amersham to/from Baker Street (semi-fast)</li>
<li>2tph Chesham to/from Aldgate (fast)</li>
<li>4tph Watford to/from Aldgate (semi-fast)</li>
<li>2tph Watford to/from Baker Street (semi-fast)</li>
<li>2tph Watford to/from Baker Street</li>
<li>7tph Uxbridge to/from Aldgate (all stations)</li>
<li>3tph Uxbridge to/from Baker Street (all stations)</li>
</ul>
<p>Note that norththbound fast and semi-fast trains return as southbound all stations services in the evening peak with the same frequency.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/London_Underground_S7_and_S8_Stock" title="London Underground S7 and S8 Stock">London Underground S7 and S8 Stock</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2307" data-file-width="3835" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg/220px-London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg/330px-London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg/440px-London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:London_MMB_C0_Metropolitan_Line_S-Stock.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
S8 Stock running between Finchley Road and Kilburn</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 26 September 2012 all services have been provided by eight-car S Stock trains<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> introduced in July 2010 to replace the A Stock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waboso_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-waboso-44">[44]</a></sup> Part of Bombardier's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movia" title="Movia">Movia</a> family, they have air-conditioning, feasible because the sub-surface tunnels, unlike tube tunnels, are able to disperse the exhausted hot air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR201012p46ff_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-MR201012p46ff-46">[46]</a></sup> They have <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_brake" title="Regenerative brake">regenerative brakes</a>, returning around 20% of their energy to the network and thus reducing energy consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a top speed of 62 miles per hour (100 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier-45">[45]</a></sup> they have fewer seats — 306 compared with 448 in the A Stock — but accommodate 697 standing passengers compared with 597 in A Stock<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[note 1]</a></sup> and have dedicated space for wheelchairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> It is planned to increase the traction voltage from the present nominal 630 V to 750 V to give better performance and allow the trains to return more energy to the network through their regenerative brakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TfL_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-TfL-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Depot">Depot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Depot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Neasden_Depot" title="Neasden Depot">Neasden Depot</a></div>
<p>The line is served by a depot at Neasden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[note 2]</a></sup> The Metropolitan Railway opened a carriage works at Neasden in 1882 and the following year the locomotive works were moved from Edgware Road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson198682.E2.80.9382_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson198682.E2.80.9382-52">[50]</a></sup> In 1904–05 the depot was refitted to take the new electric multiple units<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson1986176_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson1986176-53">[51]</a></sup> and accommodation enlarged in 1932–3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson1986281_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson1986281-54">[52]</a></sup> After the amalgamation into the LTPB, the depot was rebuilt from 1936 to 1939. The depot was upgraded in 2010–11 to make it suitable for maintenance of S Stock trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> Trains are also stabled overnight at Uxbridge, Watford, Rickmansworth and Wembley Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tfl_Key_Facts_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tfl_Key_Facts-56">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Steam_on_the_Met">Steam on the Met</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Steam on the Met">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="423" data-file-width="640" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg/220px-Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg/330px-Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg/440px-Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steam_Train_at_Amersham_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_56745.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LMS_Black_5" title="LMS Black 5">LMS Black 5</a> 44932 at Amersham in 1992</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1989, to celebrate the 100th anniversary of the opening of the Metropolitan to Chesham, the first <b>Steam on the Met</b> event took place with London Underground running two weekends of steam specials between Chesham and Watford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> The event was a success and so in 1990 London Underground ran steam between Harrow and Amersham. In 1992, to celebrate 100 years of the Met at Amersham, the event was extended to five days at the end of May. From 1994, diesel locomotive 20227, owned by the Class 20 Locomotive Society, and electric locomotive Sarah Siddons provided air braking for the coaches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1995 trains ran between Amersham and Watford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Engines used included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BR_standard_class_5" title="BR standard class 5">BR standard class 5</a> and <a href="/wiki/BR_Standard_Class_4_2-6-4T" title="BR Standard Class 4 2-6-4T">BR standard class 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/GWR_0-6-0PT" title="GWR 0-6-0PT">GWR Pannier tanks</a>. There was other <a href="/wiki/Rolling_stock" title="Rolling stock">rolling stock</a> on static display at Rickmansworth sidings. The steam trains ran between normal Metropolitan and main line services. Due to the imminent partial privatisation of LUL and the stock condition, the last steam excursion took place in 2000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2008, special trains ran on using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway_electric_locomotive" title="Metropolitan Railway electric locomotive">Metropolitan Railway electric locomotive</a> "Sarah Siddons" and diesel <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_20" title="British Rail Class 20">Class 20</a> locomotives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>To celebrate the 150th anniversary of the opening of the Metropolitan, special services ran in January 2013 using a restored 1892 "Jubilee" carriage, 1898–1900 Ashbury and Cravens bogie carriages, Metropolitan Railway milk van No.3, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway_E_Class" title="Metropolitan Railway E Class">Metropolitan Railway E Class</a> steam locomotive No. 1 and electric locomotive "Sarah Siddons".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAST_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAST-60">[58]</a></sup> Further events are planned in 2013 for Locomotive No. 1, "Sarah Siddons" and the Jubilee carriage, including a <i>Steam back on the Met</i> scheduled for May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future<span id="Upgrade_and_extension"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Croxley_rail_link.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1718" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Croxley_rail_link.png/220px-Croxley_rail_link.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Croxley_rail_link.png/330px-Croxley_rail_link.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Croxley_rail_link.png/440px-Croxley_rail_link.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Croxley_rail_link.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Diagram of the Croxley rail link proposal</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-surface_railway_upgrade">Sub-surface railway upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sub-surface railway upgrade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the introduction of S Stock, the track, electrical supply and signalling systems are being upgraded in a programme planned to increase peak-hour capacity on the line by 27 per cent by the end of 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-MR-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TfL-upgrade_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-TfL-upgrade-63">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upgradeplan_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-upgradeplan-64">[62]</a></sup> A single control room for the sub-surface railway is to be established in Hammersmith, and an <a href="/wiki/Automatic_train_control" title="Automatic train control">automatic train control</a> (ATC) system will replace signalling equipment installed from the 1940s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-MR-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR2_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-MR2-65">[63]</a></sup> Trackside signals with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_Train_Protection" title="Automatic Train Protection">Automatic Train Protection</a> (ATP) will remain on the line north of Harrow-on-the-Hill, shared with Chiltern Railways DMUs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-MR-62">[60]</a></sup> It was planned that the new signalling system would be used first on the line north of Baker Street from the end of 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MR_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-MR-62">[60]</a></sup> but the signalling contractor Bombardier was released by agreement in December 2013 and London Underground are looking for a replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> The project has been very unpopular, as seats were reduced by a third after the S-stock were introduced without a compensating increase in train services or line speeds.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Croxley_Rail_Link">Croxley Rail Link</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Croxley Rail Link">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Croxley_Rail_Link" title="Croxley Rail Link">Croxley Rail Link</a></div>
<p>The Watford Branch is planned to be rerouted from the current terminus over the disused <a href="/wiki/Watford_and_Rickmansworth_Railway" title="Watford and Rickmansworth Railway">Croxley Green branch line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction</a>. Funding was agreed in December 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> and the necessary permission was granted by the Government in July 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> Construction work is expected to span from June 2016 to January 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Croxley_plans_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Croxley_plans-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_stations">Former stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Former stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brill_branch_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="300" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Brill_branch_map.png/220px-Brill_branch_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Brill_branch_map.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brill_branch_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1924 map of the Brill and Verney Junction branches</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1145" data-file-width="1756" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg/220px-LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg/330px-LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg/440px-LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LT_loco_L92_in_1969.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
LT loco L92 at Croxley tip in 1969</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brill_Tramway" title="Brill Tramway">Brill Tramway</a> with stations <a href="/wiki/Waddesdon_Road_railway_station" title="Waddesdon Road railway station">Waddesdon Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westcott_railway_station" title="Westcott railway station">Westcott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wotton_(Metropolitan_Railway)_railway_station" title="Wotton (Metropolitan Railway) railway station">Wotton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_Siding_railway_station" title="Church Siding railway station">Church Siding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood_Siding_railway_station" title="Wood Siding railway station">Wood Siding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brill_railway_station" title="Brill railway station">Brill</a> closed in 1935. In the following year the line was cut back to Aylesbury, with <a href="/wiki/Waddesdon_railway_station" title="Waddesdon railway station">Waddesdon station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Granborough_Road_railway_station" title="Granborough Road railway station">Granborough Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winslow_Road_railway_station" title="Winslow Road railway station">Winslow Road</a> stations on the line to <a href="/wiki/Verney_Junction" title="Verney Junction">Verney Junction</a> closing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup> Initially <a href="/wiki/Verney_Junction_railway_station" title="Verney Junction railway station">Verney Junction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quainton_Road_railway_station" title="Quainton Road railway station">Quainton Road</a> remained open, with main line services provided by the LNER.</p>
<p>In 1939 the <a href="/wiki/Stanmore_tube_station" title="Stanmore tube station">Stanmore</a> branch and the stopping service between Finchley Road and Wembley Park were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Bakerloo_line" title="Bakerloo line">Bakerloo line</a>. On the St John's Wood section, <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_tube_station" title="Lord's tube station">Lord's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marlborough_Road_tube_station" title="Marlborough Road tube station">Marlborough Road</a> stations were replaced by <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Wood_tube_station" title="St. John's Wood tube station">St. John's Wood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Cottage_tube_station" title="Swiss Cottage tube station">Swiss Cottage</a> replaced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Cottage_(Metropolitan_line)_tube_station" title="Swiss Cottage (Metropolitan line) tube station">the Metropolitan line station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198751_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198751-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup> The Bakerloo line service to Stanmore was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line" title="Jubilee line">Jubilee line</a> when that line opened in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen198763_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen198763-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1961, when steam locomotives were replaced and the line was electrified to Amersham, the Underground service to <a href="/wiki/Great_Missenden_railway_station" title="Great Missenden railway station">Great Missenden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wendover_railway_station" title="Wendover railway station">Wendover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stoke_Mandeville_railway_station" title="Stoke Mandeville railway station">Stoke Mandeville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aylesbury_railway_station" title="Aylesbury railway station">Aylesbury</a> was withdrawn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_14-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goods-only_branches">Goods-only branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_line&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Goods-only branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between Moor Park and Croxley, a short branch ran south-east off the Watford branch near its junction with the main line to Croxley Tip, a rubbish dump beside the Grand Union Canal. This site began as a gravel loading point before becoming used by the railway to dump waste such as old ballast and waste from <a href="/wiki/Neasden_Power_Station" title="Neasden Power Station">Neasden power station</a>. This route, never used for passenger traffic, continued to be used by London Transport's small fleet of steam engines until 1971, when diesels replaced them. The branch closed some time after this, although a section of the spur line remained visible from a passing train.</p>
<p>A second short branch line, known as the <a href="/wiki/Halton_Railway" title="Halton Railway">Halton Railway</a>, served <a href="/wiki/RAF_Halton" title="RAF Halton">RAF Halton</a> near Wendover, across the <a href="/wiki/Wendover_Arm_Canal" title="Wendover Arm Canal">Wendover Arm</a> of the Grand Union Canal. The line was built during the First World War and closed in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Halton_Railway_MOD_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Halton_Railway_MOD-70">[68]</a></sup> The trackbed is now a footpath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Wendover_Arm:_Linear_and_Circular_Walks_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Wendover_Arm:_Linear_and_Circular_Walks-71">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although not operated by Metropolitan passenger services, the line from South Harrow to Rayners Lane was built by the Metropolitan railway as the <a href="/wiki/District_Railway" title="District Railway">District Railway</a> was in financial difficulties at the time. This included a short branch on viaduct to a gas works, part of which is still visible. Other minor freight connections along the line once included connections to the Midland main line at Finchley Road.</p>
<p>A single-track spur from a small yard between Ickenham and Ruislip stations connects to <a href="/wiki/Ruislip_depot" title="Ruislip depot">Ruislip Depot</a> of the Central line. This line is used for engineering and empty stock transfers, although occasional plans suggest extending the Central line into Uxbridge by upgrading the connection. It was built in 1973.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
